Prioritizing Certainty Over Hypothesis
Buti states the total contradiction and gives the rational principle for resolving it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational principle that when a definitive truth contradicts a theoretical hypothesis, the truth must be upheld and the hypothesis set aside.

Core Idea
Certain truth abrogates hypothesis, never the reverse.

In this passage, Buti confronts a key challenge: the theory of evolution seems to conflict with the Islamic account of man's origin. He sets the stage by stating this contradiction and then articulates a universal rational principle for resolving such conflicts. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the contradiction
Buti states that the Islamic truth about man's origin completely contradicts the theory of evolution. Note the phrase 'مناقضة كلية' (total contradiction).
3
Understand the rational principle
Buti lays down the principle: when a scientific truth (حقيقة علمية) contradicts a theoretical issue (مسألة نظرية), the truth must survive and the theory must be abrogated. Ask yourself why this is the rational position.
This principle is key to the entire argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصير نظرية النشوء والارتقاء أمام هذه الحقيقة

وكما ترى، فإن هذه الحقيقة القطعية التي يجب على المسلم الاعتقاد بها تتناقض مناقضة كلية مع ما يسمى بنظرية النشوء والارتقاء، التي تتبنى فرضية تاريخية أخرى عن الإنسان، وهي أنه تسلسل ضمن حلقات مختلفة من التطور النوعي، تدرج فيها من البسيط إلى المعقد، ومن البدائية إلى الرقي، في كل من الشكل والفكر معاً. فما موقف المسلم من هذا التناقض والخلاف؟

والجواب: أن موقفه ينبغي أن يكون الموقف ذاته الذي يتخذه أي عاقل لدى تناقض حقيقة علمية مع مسألة نظرية. إذ لا ريب أن الحقيقة العلمية هي التي ينبغي أن يكتب لها البقاء، ولا مناص من نسخ النظرية مادامت مناقضة لتلك الحقيقة لا يمكن جمعها معها.

وعلينا الآن أن نوضح (مجدداً) كيف أن الحكم الذي ذكرناه عن واقع الإنسان، حقيقة علمية ثابتة، بينما الحكم بتطور الإنسان تطوراً نوعياً مجرد نظرية بل فرضية ليس من حولها أي برهان علمي.

وينبغي أن تعلم أولاً، أن هذه المسألة ليست مما يتعلق بالمحسوسات والمشاهدات، فلا مطمع في أن تبحث لها عن دليل من التجربة المحسوسة المشاهدة. ذلك لأن البحث ليس متعلقاً بالإنسان الحالي، حتى يكون الموضوع خاضعاً لمجهر التجربة والمشاهدة، وإنما هو متعلق باكتشاف ناحية تاريخية فيه. مرت وانطوت. وكل ما يمكن الاستعانة به في البحث، من المستحاثات ووجوه الشبه بين الإنسان وحيوانات أخرى وغير ذلك، إنما هو من وسائل البحث الاستردادي وسبيل من سبل الفرض والتوسم، وشتان بين هذه الوسائل وبرهان التجربة والمشاهدة.

ثم إن المسألة ليست أيضاً مما يخضع لقانون التلازم أو القياس الصحيح القائمين على أساس الاستقراء التام، إذ هي كما قلنا محاولة استكشاف لتاريخ بعيد موغل في القدم ليس بيننا وبينه أي برهان علمي قاطع.

ولو أن المسألة وقفت عند هذا الحد، لالتزمنا جانب الشك أو الظن المجرد، دون أن تخضع عقولنا لأي فرضية أو نظرية تحتمل الخطأ والصواب.

ولكنها لم تقف عند هذا الحد، فقد كشف عنها الخبر اليقيني المتواتر الذي فرغنا من عرضه وبيانه.

وقد علمت أن مصدر الخبر صريح كلام القرآن. وعلمت فيما مضى أن القرآن ليس كلام محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام بل هو كلام الله عز وجل بالبرهان القطعي الذي مر بيانه. وعلمت قبل ذلك البرهان القطعي على وجود الله عز وجل.

فكان لا بد إذاً من اليقين بأن ما تضمنه خبر القرآن هو الحق لأنه كلام الله عز وجل، يتحدث بنفسه عن كيفية خلقه للإنسان.

فقد ثبت إذاً أن حديث الإسلام عن أصل الإنسان حقيقة علمية قاطعة.

أما حديث داروين، فهو ليس أكثر من نظرية وفرضية باعترافه وباتفاق سائر العلماء الآخرين سواء منهم من أيده أم خالفه. وليست نظريته عن أصل الأنواع، إلا حلقة في سلسلة نظريات متلاحقة مختلفة، كلها تفرض أن الحياة تطورت على وجه هذه الأرض تطوراً آلياً، ثم تتفرق عن بعضها في طرائق مختلفة لتفسير هذا التطور وتحليله.
The fate of the theory of evolution in the face of this truth

And as you see, this definitive truth which the Muslim must believe contradicts completely what is called the theory of evolution, which adopts another historical hypothesis about man, namely that he is a sequence within different rings of specific evolution, progressing in it from simple to complex, and from primitiveness to advancement, in both form and thought together. So what is the Muslim's position regarding this contradiction and disagreement?

And the answer: that his position should be the same position that any rational person takes when a scientific truth contradicts a theoretical issue. For there is no doubt that the scientific truth is what should survive, and there is no escape from abrogating the theory as long as it contradicts that truth and cannot be reconciled with it.

And we must now clarify (again) how the judgment we mentioned about the reality of man is a fixed scientific truth, while the judgment of man's specific evolution is merely a theory, rather a hypothesis that has no scientific proof around it.

And you should know first, that this issue is not among sensory matters and observations, so there is no hope of seeking for it a proof from observed sensory experiment. That is because the research is not related to current man, such that the subject would be subject to the microscope of experiment and observation, but rather it is related to discovering a historical aspect in him that has passed and closed. And all that can be used in research, from fossils and similarities between man and other animals and so on, are only means of retrospective research and a way of hypothesizing and conjecture, and how far these means are from the proof of experiment and observation.

Then, the issue is also not subject to the law of correlation or sound analogy based on complete induction, since it is, as we said, an attempt to explore a distant, ancient history between us and which there is no decisive scientific proof.

And if the issue had stopped at this limit, we would have adhered to the side of doubt or mere conjecture, without subjecting our minds to any hypothesis or theory that carries the possibility of error and correctness.

But it did not stop at this limit, for the certain mutawatir report that we have finished presenting and explaining has disclosed it.

And you have known that the source of the report is the explicit speech of the Quran. And you have known previously that the Quran is not the speech of Muhammad, peace be upon him, but rather it is the speech of God Almighty by the definitive proof whose explanation has passed. And you knew before that the definitive proof of the existence of God Almighty.

Thus it must be certain that what the report of the Quran contains is the truth because it is the speech of God Almighty, speaking Himself about the manner of His creation of man.

So it is established, therefore, that Islam's account of the origin of man is a definitive scientific truth.

As for Darwin's account, it is nothing more than a theory and hypothesis by his own admission and by agreement of all other scholars, whether among those who supported him or opposed him. And his theory of the origin of species is nothing but a link in a series of successive different theories, all of which assume that life evolved on the face of this earth mechanically, then they diverge in different ways to explain and analyze this evolution.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument refuting the theory of evolution and establishing the Islamic account of man's origin as definitive truth. The author, Buti, begins by stating the central contradiction: the definitive Islamic truth about man's creation contradicts the evolutionary hypothesis. He then asks what the Muslim's position should be.

Buti answers by articulating a general principle: when a scientific truth conflicts with a theoretical question, the rational person must favor the scientific truth. The scientific truth survives, and the theory must be set aside since it cannot be reconciled with the truth.

He then clarifies that the Islamic judgment about man is a fixed scientific truth, while the idea of human evolution is merely a theory—indeed, a hypothesis without scientific proof.

Buti proceeds to explain why this is not an empirical matter: the question is not about contemporary humans, who could be observed, but about a past historical event. Therefore, means like fossils and similarities are only tools of retrospective research and conjecture, not experimental proof. He further argues that the issue does not fall under laws of correlation or sound analogy based on complete induction, because it is an attempt to explore an ancient history with no decisive scientific proof.

If the matter rested there, Buti says, we would be left with doubt or conjecture. However, it does not rest there because the certain mutawatir report (the Quran) has disclosed the truth about man's origin. The source of this report is the explicit speech of the Quran, which has been proven to be the speech of God, not of Muhammad, through a definitive proof. And that proof itself rests on the definitive proof of God's existence.

Therefore, Buti concludes, it is necessary to be certain that the Quran's report is the truth, as it is God's own speech about His creation of man. Hence, Islam's account of man's origin is a definitive scientific truth.

In contrast, Darwin's account is nothing more than a theory and a hypothesis, acknowledged as such by Darwin himself and by all other scientists, supporters and opponents alike. Darwin's theory of the origin of species is merely one link in a chain of successive, differing theories that all assume life evolved mechanically, diverging only in their explanations of that evolution.

This passage thus functions as a refutation of evolution and a defense of the Quranic narrative as the only certain truth on this matter. The argument proceeds step by step: establishing the conflict, stating the principle of preferring certainty over theory, showing the lack of empirical evidence for evolution, demonstrating the definitive nature of the Quranic report, and finally contrasting the two positions.

Key Terms
نظرية النشوء والارتقاء
حقيقة قطعية
مسألة نظرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the theory of evolution can be reconciled with the Islamic account of creation.
Correction: Buti states they are in total contradiction (مناقضة كلية) and cannot be reconciled (لا يمكن جمعها معها).

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what should be done when a scientific truth contradicts a theoretical hypothesis?
A) The hypothesis should be retained and the truth reconsidered.
B) Both should be accepted as equally valid.
C) The truth should be preserved and the hypothesis abrogated.
D) The truth should be rejected if it conflicts with majority opinion.

Key Takeaway
When a definitive truth contradicts a hypothesis, the rational position is to uphold the truth and discard the hypothesis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a contradiction between what you know from revelation and your own reasoning or popular theories, do you instinctively prioritize the revealed truth, or do you feel pressured to accommodate the theory? Today, commit to letting the definitive truth abrogate any hypothesis that opposes it, no matter how widely accepted.
?
Is there any belief or assumption you hold that you have never subjected to the test of certainty? Identify one area where you have allowed a speculative idea to coexist with a clear truth from Allah. Will you now let the truth abrogate that assumption?
?
The rational principle Buti invokes is universal: truth abrogates hypothesis. In your daily life, do you apply this consistently? For example, when a worldly ambition contradicts a command of Allah, which do you treat as the hypothesis to be discarded? Ask Allah for the strength to always side with the truth.

The Quranic Account: Certainty Over Conjecture
Buti argues that the Quranic report provides certain knowledge about man's origin, while Darwin's theory remains a mere hypothesis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti considers the Islamic account of man's origin to be a definitive truth based on the certain report of the Quran, while Darwin's theory remains mere hypothesis.

Core Idea
Revelation provides certainty where scientific conjecture yields only doubt.

After arguing that evolution lacks empirical and inductive proof, Buti now introduces the key factor that changes the picture: the certain report from the Quran. This report, being from God, provides a level of certainty that no hypothesis can match. Let's see how he establishes this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Understand the role of the mutawatir report
Buti says that without revelation we would be left in doubt, but the certain mutawatir report (the Quran) has disclosed the truth. Note how he ties this to previous proofs about the Quran being God's speech.
3
Contrast with Darwin's hypothesis
Buti concludes by contrasting the certainty of the Quranic account with Darwin's theory, which he describes as merely a hypothesis by admission of its own proponents.
This reinforces the principle from the previous lesson.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصير نظرية النشوء والارتقاء أمام هذه الحقيقة

وكما ترى، فإن هذه الحقيقة القطعية التي يجب على المسلم الاعتقاد بها تتناقض مناقضة كلية مع ما يسمى بنظرية النشوء والارتقاء، التي تتبنى فرضية تاريخية أخرى عن الإنسان، وهي أنه تسلسل ضمن حلقات مختلفة من التطور النوعي، تدرج فيها من البسيط إلى المعقد، ومن البدائية إلى الرقي، في كل من الشكل والفكر معاً. فما موقف المسلم من هذا التناقض والخلاف؟

والجواب: أن موقفه ينبغي أن يكون الموقف ذاته الذي يتخذه أي عاقل لدى تناقض حقيقة علمية مع مسألة نظرية. إذ لا ريب أن الحقيقة العلمية هي التي ينبغي أن يكتب لها البقاء، ولا مناص من نسخ النظرية مادامت مناقضة لتلك الحقيقة لا يمكن جمعها معها.

وعلينا الآن أن نوضح (مجدداً) كيف أن الحكم الذي ذكرناه عن واقع الإنسان، حقيقة علمية ثابتة، بينما الحكم بتطور الإنسان تطوراً نوعياً مجرد نظرية بل فرضية ليس من حولها أي برهان علمي.

وينبغي أن تعلم أولاً، أن هذه المسألة ليست مما يتعلق بالمحسوسات والمشاهدات، فلا مطمع في أن تبحث لها عن دليل من التجربة المحسوسة المشاهدة. ذلك لأن البحث ليس متعلقاً بالإنسان الحالي، حتى يكون الموضوع خاضعاً لمجهر التجربة والمشاهدة، وإنما هو متعلق باكتشاف ناحية تاريخية فيه. مرت وانطوت. وكل ما يمكن الاستعانة به في البحث، من المستحاثات ووجوه الشبه بين الإنسان وحيوانات أخرى وغير ذلك، إنما هو من وسائل البحث الاستردادي وسبيل من سبل الفرض والتوسم، وشتان بين هذه الوسائل وبرهان التجربة والمشاهدة.

ثم إن المسألة ليست أيضاً مما يخضع لقانون التلازم أو القياس الصحيح القائمين على أساس الاستقراء التام، إذ هي كما قلنا محاولة استكشاف لتاريخ بعيد موغل في القدم ليس بيننا وبينه أي برهان علمي قاطع.

ولو أن المسألة وقفت عند هذا الحد، لالتزمنا جانب الشك أو الظن المجرد، دون أن تخضع عقولنا لأي فرضية أو نظرية تحتمل الخطأ والصواب.

ولكنها لم تقف عند هذا الحد، فقد كشف عنها الخبر اليقيني المتواتر الذي فرغنا من عرضه وبيانه.

وقد علمت أن مصدر الخبر صريح كلام القرآن. وعلمت فيما مضى أن القرآن ليس كلام محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام بل هو كلام الله عز وجل بالبرهان القطعي الذي مر بيانه. وعلمت قبل ذلك البرهان القطعي على وجود الله عز وجل.

فكان لا بد إذاً من اليقين بأن ما تضمنه خبر القرآن هو الحق لأنه كلام الله عز وجل، يتحدث بنفسه عن كيفية خلقه للإنسان.

فقد ثبت إذاً أن حديث الإسلام عن أصل الإنسان حقيقة علمية قاطعة.

أما حديث داروين، فهو ليس أكثر من نظرية وفرضية باعترافه وباتفاق سائر العلماء الآخرين سواء منهم من أيده أم خالفه. وليست نظريته عن أصل الأنواع، إلا حلقة في سلسلة نظريات متلاحقة مختلفة، كلها تفرض أن الحياة تطورت على وجه هذه الأرض تطوراً آلياً، ثم تتفرق عن بعضها في طرائق مختلفة لتفسير هذا التطور وتحليله.
The fate of the theory of evolution in the face of this truth

And as you see, this definitive truth which the Muslim must believe contradicts completely what is called the theory of evolution, which adopts another historical hypothesis about man, namely that he is a sequence within different rings of specific evolution, progressing in it from simple to complex, and from primitiveness to advancement, in both form and thought together. So what is the Muslim's position regarding this contradiction and disagreement?

And the answer: that his position should be the same position that any rational person takes when a scientific truth contradicts a theoretical issue. For there is no doubt that the scientific truth is what should survive, and there is no escape from abrogating the theory as long as it contradicts that truth and cannot be reconciled with it.

And we must now clarify (again) how the judgment we mentioned about the reality of man is a fixed scientific truth, while the judgment of man's specific evolution is merely a theory, rather a hypothesis that has no scientific proof around it.

And you should know first, that this issue is not among sensory matters and observations, so there is no hope of seeking for it a proof from observed sensory experiment. That is because the research is not related to current man, such that the subject would be subject to the microscope of experiment and observation, but rather it is related to discovering a historical aspect in him that has passed and closed. And all that can be used in research, from fossils and similarities between man and other animals and so on, are only means of retrospective research and a way of hypothesizing and conjecture, and how far these means are from the proof of experiment and observation.

Then, the issue is also not subject to the law of correlation or sound analogy based on complete induction, since it is, as we said, an attempt to explore a distant, ancient history between us and which there is no decisive scientific proof.

And if the issue had stopped at this limit, we would have adhered to the side of doubt or mere conjecture, without subjecting our minds to any hypothesis or theory that carries the possibility of error and correctness.

But it did not stop at this limit, for the certain mutawatir report that we have finished presenting and explaining has disclosed it.

And you have known that the source of the report is the explicit speech of the Quran. And you have known previously that the Quran is not the speech of Muhammad, peace be upon him, but rather it is the speech of God Almighty by the definitive proof whose explanation has passed. And you knew before that the definitive proof of the existence of God Almighty.

Thus it must be certain that what the report of the Quran contains is the truth because it is the speech of God Almighty, speaking Himself about the manner of His creation of man.

So it is established, therefore, that Islam's account of the origin of man is a definitive scientific truth.

As for Darwin's account, it is nothing more than a theory and hypothesis by his own admission and by agreement of all other scholars, whether among those who supported him or opposed him. And his theory of the origin of species is nothing but a link in a series of successive different theories, all of which assume that life evolved on the face of this earth mechanically, then they diverge in different ways to explain and analyze this evolution.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument refuting the theory of evolution and establishing the Islamic account of man's origin as definitive truth. The author, Buti, begins by stating the central contradiction: the definitive Islamic truth about man's creation contradicts the evolutionary hypothesis. He then asks what the Muslim's position should be.

Buti answers by articulating a general principle: when a scientific truth conflicts with a theoretical question, the rational person must favor the scientific truth. The scientific truth survives, and the theory must be set aside since it cannot be reconciled with the truth.

He then clarifies that the Islamic judgment about man is a fixed scientific truth, while the idea of human evolution is merely a theory—indeed, a hypothesis without scientific proof.

Buti proceeds to explain why this is not an empirical matter: the question is not about contemporary humans, who could be observed, but about a past historical event. Therefore, means like fossils and similarities are only tools of retrospective research and conjecture, not experimental proof. He further argues that the issue does not fall under laws of correlation or sound analogy based on complete induction, because it is an attempt to explore an ancient history with no decisive scientific proof.

If the matter rested there, Buti says, we would be left with doubt or conjecture. However, it does not rest there because the certain mutawatir report (the Quran) has disclosed the truth about man's origin. The source of this report is the explicit speech of the Quran, which has been proven to be the speech of God, not of Muhammad, through a definitive proof. And that proof itself rests on the definitive proof of God's existence.

Therefore, Buti concludes, it is necessary to be certain that the Quran's report is the truth, as it is God's own speech about His creation of man. Hence, Islam's account of man's origin is a definitive scientific truth.

In contrast, Darwin's account is nothing more than a theory and a hypothesis, acknowledged as such by Darwin himself and by all other scientists, supporters and opponents alike. Darwin's theory of the origin of species is merely one link in a chain of successive, differing theories that all assume life evolved mechanically, diverging only in their explanations of that evolution.

This passage thus functions as a refutation of evolution and a defense of the Quranic narrative as the only certain truth on this matter. The argument proceeds step by step: establishing the conflict, stating the principle of preferring certainty over theory, showing the lack of empirical evidence for evolution, demonstrating the definitive nature of the Quranic report, and finally contrasting the two positions.

Key Terms
خبر يقيني متواتر
برهان قطعي
نظرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the theory of evolution is a scientifically proven fact.
Correction: Buti argues it is a hypothesis without scientific proof, while the Quranic account is certain truth.

Checkpoint
What does Buti say would be our position if we only had scientific evidence about man's origin, without revelation?
A) We would have certainty.
B) We would be left with doubt and conjecture.
C) We would accept Darwin's theory.
D) We would reject all possibilities.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic report about man's origin is a definitive truth because it comes from God, whereas Darwin's theory remains mere hypothesis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim the Quran is Allah’s speech. But does your daily certainty about the unseen—like life after death—match the definitive truth it claims, or do you treat it as a mere theory? What would it take for you to live as if the Quran is the only definitive truth that matters?
?
Where in your life have you settled for 'mere conjecture' about Allah’s commands when decisive revelation is available? Write down one area where you will replace human opinion with divine certainty starting today.
?
Darwin’s theory is probabilistic; revelation is definitive. Yet, how often do you base your hopes and fears on probabilities instead of on the absolute truth of Allah’s word? Will you let tonight’s reflection be a turning point where you choose certainty over conjecture?

Why Empirical Science Cannot Determine Human Origin
Buti enumerates the limitations of scientific methods for ancient history.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why empirical science, based on induction and observation, cannot provide certain knowledge about the distant origin of humanity.

Core Idea
Science cannot prove the distant past; it can only hypothesize.

Dr. Buti begins by examining the nature of scientific evidence regarding human origin. He argues that the scientific methods of experiment, observation, and induction are insufficient to establish certainty about events in the remote past. Instead, such inquiries remain in the realm of hypothesis and conjecture.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how Buti contrasts 'retrospective' methods with empirical proof.
2
Identify the limits of science
Buti lists several scientific methods—experiment, observation, correlation, syllogism, complete induction—and explains why they fail for the distant past. Find these terms and understand his reasoning.
Key phrase: 'ليس بيننا وبينه أي برهان علمي قاطع' (no decisive scientific proof).
3
Understand the consequence
If science cannot provide certainty, what remains? Buti says we would be left with doubt or pure conjecture, not subjecting our minds to any hypothesis. This sets up the need for revelation.

Source Text

The retrospective and one of the ways of hypothesis and conjecture, and how different are these means from the proof of experiment and observation. Then the issue is not also subject to the law of correlation or the correct syllogism based on complete induction, for it is, as we said, an attempt to explore a distant history deeply rooted in antiquity with no decisive scientific proof between us and it. And if the issue had stopped at this limit, we would have adhered to the side of doubt or pure conjecture, without our minds being subject to any hypothesis or theory that bears the possibility of error and correctness. But it did not stop at this limit, for the certain recurrent report (al-khabar al-yaqīnī al-mutawātir) that we have already presented and explained revealed it. And you know that the source of the report is the explicit speech of the Qur'an. And you knew before that the Qur'an is not the speech of Muhammad (peace be upon him) but rather the speech of God Almighty, with the decisive proof (al-burhān al-qaṭʿī) that has already been explained. And you knew before that the decisive proof of the existence of God Almighty. So it was necessary, therefore, to be certain that what the Qur'an's report contains is the truth, because it is the speech of God Almighty, speaking Himself about how He created man. Thus it is established that the Islamic account of the origin of man is a decisive scientific truth. As for Darwin's account, it is nothing more than a theory and hypothesis, by his own admission and by agreement of all other scholars, whether supporters or opponents, and his theory of the origin of species is nothing but a link in a chain of successive different theories, all assuming that life developed on the face of this earth automatically, then diverging from each other in various ways to interpret and analyze this development.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is an argument establishing the certainty of the Islamic account of human origin over empirical science and Darwinian theory. The author begins by characterizing the retrospective approach as only conjecture, far removed from empirical proof. He then asserts that the question of human origin is not subject to the laws of correlation or correct syllogism based on complete induction, because it concerns an ancient past with no decisive scientific evidence. If it were only that, we would be left in doubt. However, the certain recurrent report (al-khabar al-mutawātir) of the Qur'an has revealed it. The author reminds us that this report is the explicit speech of the Qur'an, which has been proven decisively to be God's speech, not Muhammad's, and that God's existence is also decisively proven. Therefore, what the Qur'an says is necessarily true, as it is God's own account of creating man. Hence, the Islamic account is a decisive scientific truth. In contrast, Darwin's theory is presented as mere hypothesis and conjecture, admitted even by its proponents, and is just one in a series of evolving theories. The argument flows from the limitation of empirical science to the necessity of revelation, culminating in a sharp contrast between Islamic certainty and Darwinian conjecture.

According to the passage, why are empirical scientific methods insufficient to determine human origin?
A) Because the issue is too complex for experiment
B) Because there is no decisive scientific proof from that distant past
C) Because the Qur'an has already provided the answer
D) Because scientists disagree among themselves

Key Takeaway
Empirical science cannot settle questions about the unique, unobserved past; it only produces hypotheses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often encounter scientific claims about human origins that are presented as certain. After reading this lesson, what assumptions about science do you need to question? Will you accept a claim as fact just because it comes from a scientist, or will you demand to know the basis of evidence? This lesson is a call to intellectual integrity. Commit to investigating the epistemological foundations of any claim before you let it shape your worldview.
?
Buti argues that without proof, the only rational stance is doubt or conjecture. But in your own life, how often do you hold beliefs about the past—your personal history or the history of your community—without absolute proof? How does this lesson challenge you to seek certainty from the right sources? What will you do today to ground your beliefs in what is truly known?
?
Consider a belief you hold about your own origins. Is it based on empirical science or on revelation? Buti shows that science cannot give certainty about the distant past. Are you willing to place your trust in the divine revelation that alone can speak authoritatively? This is not an academic exercise; it is a question of the foundation of your faith. Will you let the limitations of science drive you to seek knowledge from the Quran and Sunnah?

The Decisive Certainty of the Qur'anic Account of Human Origin
Buti establishes the certainty of the Islamic account via revelation and contrasts it with Darwinian theory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic account of human origin, transmitted through a mutawatir report and supported by decisive proofs, provides absolute certainty, unlike Darwin's theory.

Core Idea
The Qur'an gives certain knowledge of creation; Darwin offers mere theory.

Having shown the limits of science, Buti now presents the alternative: divine revelation. He reminds us of the chain of proofs establishing the Qur'an as God's speech and God's existence, concluding that the Islamic account is decisive truth. In stark contrast, Darwinian theory remains hypothesis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the shift from 'if the issue had stopped' to 'but it did not stop'.
2
Trace the chain of certainty
Buti mentions three things known from before: the khabar mutawatir, that the Qur'an is God's speech (by decisive proof), and the decisive proof of God's existence. Understand how each link leads to certainty.
Key phrase: 'فكان لا بد إذاً من اليقين' (so it was necessary to be certain).
3
Contrast with Darwin's theory
Buti explicitly contrasts the Islamic account as 'decisive scientific truth' with Darwin's account as 'nothing more than a theory and hypothesis'. Note the reasons: admission by Darwin himself and agreement of scholars.
Darwin's theory is part of a chain of evolving theories, each assuming automatic evolution.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as though the Qur'an's account of creation is certain, or do you secretly entertain doubt when confronted with scientific theories that contradict it? What would change if you fully internalized that every word of the Qur'an is the speech of God, spoken by Him directly about how He created you?
?
Buti notes that Darwin himself admitted his account is only a theory. When you hear evolutionary theory presented as undeniable fact in educational or popular settings, does your heart remain firm in the certainty of revelation, or does it waver? What specific verse or proof do you lean on to anchor your conviction?
?
You might have thought that because there are multiple interpretations of the Qur'an, the creation account is open to doubt. But Buti insists it is decisive. Are you willing to submit to the clear text even when it clashes with your own assumptions or the prevailing worldview? What is holding you back from absolute certainty in the Qur'an's report about your origins?

Proof of Angels from Revelation and Ruling on Denial
Proof of angels' existence through revealed texts and ruling on denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the existence of angels is established by definitive textual proof from the Quran and Sunnah, and that denying their existence constitutes disbelief.

Core Idea
Angels exist — and denying them is kufr.

This lesson presents the Islamic evidence for the existence of angels. The author draws on the Qur'an and authentic Hadith to show that the existence of angels is a matter of definitive certainty, and he clarifies the grave ruling for those who reject it.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to get the author's flow.
2
Locate the primary proof
The author states that the proof is the 'truthful, mutawātir report'. Find this phrase and understand what it means.
Mutawātir means transmitted by so many reliable narrators that it yields certain knowledge.
3
Observe the cited evidence
Notice the two Quranic verses (2:285, 16:2) and the Hadith of Jibril. Why does the author choose these?
These texts directly command belief in angels as part of faith.
4
Understand the definitive nature
The author says the proof is 'dalīl qatʻ' — definitive and immune to doubt. What does that imply for the strength of the evidence?
5
Learn the ruling on denial
The author states that denial is kufr by consensus and by Quranic text. Also note the additional argument linking prophethood and angels.
Denying angels undermines belief in the Quran and prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحديث في هذا المقام يتعلق بوجودهم ، وصفاتهم ، ووظائف بعضهم . فأما وجودهم ، فقد دلّ عليه الخبر الصادق المتواتر عن الله جل جلاله وعن رسوله عليه الصلاة والسلام . فأما الوارد من ذلك عن الله جل جلاله فقوله : ﴿ آمَنَ الرَّسُولُ بِمَا أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ رَبِّهِ وَالْمُؤْمِنُونَ كُلٌّ آمَنَ بِاللَّهِ وَمَلائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ ﴾ [ البقرة : ۲۸۵ ] وقوله : ﴿ هُوَ يُنَزِّلُ الْمَلائِكَةَ بِالرُّوحِ مِنْ أَمْرِهِ عَلَى مَنْ يَشَاءُ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ أَنْ أَنْذِرُوا أَنَّهُ لا إِلَهَ إِلا أَنَا فَاتَّقُونِ ﴾ [النحل : ٢ ] . ذلك وأما الوارد عن رسول الله فقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لجبريل في الحديث المعروف عن عمر بن الخطاب ، عندما سأله جبريل عن الإيمان : « أن تؤمن بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخر وتؤمن بالقدر خيره وشره » (رواه مسلم وروى البخاري نحوه). وفي كل من القرآن والسنة الصحيحة نصوص كثيرة أخرى ، تخبر بصريح العبارة عن وجود الملائكة . وبذلك تعلم أن وجودهم ثابت بدليل القطع الذي لا يمكن أن يلحقه شك أو ريب . ومن هنا كان إنكار وجودهم كفراً بإجماع المسلمين بل بنص قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَنْ يَكْفُرْ بِاللَّهِ وَمَلائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الآخِرِ فَقَدْ ضَلَّ ضَلالاً بَعِيداً ﴾ [ النساء : ١٣٦ ] على أن الإيمان بنبوة محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ونزول القرآن عليه يستلزم الإيمان بالملائكة ، فإنكار وجودهم إنكار للنبوة وللقرآن معاً .
And the discussion in this context concerns their existence, their attributes, and the functions of some of them. As for their existence, the truthful, mutawātir report from God – Exalted is His Majesty – and from His Messenger – peace and blessings be upon him – has indicated it. As for what is transmitted from God – Exalted is His Majesty – is His statement: {The Messenger has believed in what was revealed to him from his Lord, and the believers; all have believed in God, His angels, His books, and His messengers} [Al-Baqarah 2:285], and His statement: {He sends down the angels with the spirit [the revelation] of His command upon whom He wills of His servants, [saying]: 'Warn that there is no deity except Me, so fear Me'} [An-Nahl 16:2]. And as for what is transmitted from the Messenger of God – peace and blessings be upon him – is his statement to Gabriel in the well-known hadith from Umar ibn al-Khattab, when Gabriel asked him about faith: 'That you believe in God, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, and that you believe in divine decree, its good and its evil' (narrated by Muslim and al-Bukhari narrated similarly). And in both the Quran and the authentic Sunnah there are many other texts that declare in clear wording the existence of angels. And by that you know that their existence is established by a definitive proof that cannot be affected by doubt or skepticism. Hence, denying their existence is disbelief by consensus of the Muslims, nay, by the text of God's statement: {And whoever disbelieves in God, His angels, His books, His messengers, and the Last Day has certainly gone far astray} [An-Nisa 4:136], and also because belief in the prophethood of Muhammad – peace and blessings be upon him – and the revelation of the Quran upon him necessitates belief in the angels, so denying their existence is a denial of prophethood and the Quran together.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a proof text combined with a theological ruling. The author begins by narrowing the scope of the discussion to three aspects: existence, attributes, and functions of angels. Then he addresses existence first. The proof is the 'truthful, mutawātir report' from God and His Messenger. He cites two Quranic verses: Al-Baqarah 2:285, which mentions belief in angels as part of faith, and An-Nahl 16:2, which describes God sending angels with revelation. From the Sunnah, he cites the famous hadith of Gabriel where the Prophet defines faith to include belief in angels. He notes that this hadith is narrated by Muslim and similar by Bukhari. After citing these primary texts, he states that there are many other texts in both sources. Consequently, the existence of angels is established by a definitive proof (dalīl qaṭʻ) immune to doubt. He then delivers the ruling: denial is disbelief (kufr) by consensus of Muslims and by the explicit text of Quran 4:136, which counts disbelief in angels as part of overall disbelief. Finally, he adds an additional argument: belief in the prophethood of Muhammad and the Quran logically necessitates belief in angels, because the Quran was brought by Gabriel. Hence, denying angels undermines both prophethood and the Quran.

دليل القطع
كفر
إجماع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that angels' existence can only be known through reason, not revelation.
Correction: The author stresses that the proof is definitive textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, not rational argument alone.

Checkpoint

The existence of angels is proven by definitive textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, and denying it is an act of disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

(2:285) with presence of heart tonight, reflecting on the angels.
?
Denial of angels is kufr. But consider: do I ever neglect the reality of angels in my daily life—for example, forgetting that they record my every word and deed? Before you sleep tonight, reflect on your day's actions: if you knew the recording angels were noting everything, what would you have done differently? Make a firm intention to change that one thing tomorrow.

Detailed vs General Knowledge of Angels
Author distinguishes between detailed and general knowledge of angelic attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why detailed knowledge of angelic attributes is not required in Islam, and how general knowledge of their attributes is derived from the Quran.

Core Idea
Belief in angelic attributes is limited to general Quranic descriptions, not speculative details.

The author addresses a common question: how much must Muslims believe about angels? He explains that while we cannot know every detail, the Quran provides sufficient general attributes for belief. This lesson explores the epistemological distinction between detailed and general knowledge of angelic attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how the author presents two categories: detailed knowledge (impossible) and general knowledge (possible).
The author uses a contrast structure: 'أما... فـ' for detailed, then 'وأما... فـ' for general.
2
Understand the reason for limitation
The author argues that detailed knowledge depends on reports, and no mutawātir reports have reached us. That is why detailed belief is not obligatory.
Mutawātir means reports transmitted by many independent chains, guaranteeing certainty.
3
Identify the source for general knowledge
General knowledge is derived from the Quran, which is a truthful report. The author then provides four verses as examples of general attributes.
These verses describe angels as obedient, honored servants with wings, etc.
4
Reflect on the practical implication
The key takeaway is that Muslims are not required to research or believe in every reported detail about angels; only general attributes from definitive sources are obligatory.
This prevents unnecessary speculation and keeps faith grounded in clear revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما صفاتهم ، فإن تفصيل القول في ذلك مما لا سبيل إليه ، إذ هي مما لا يمكن معرفته إلا عن طريق الأخبار ، ولم يصل إلينا من الأخبار الصادقة المتواترة ما يكشف لنا عن أحوالهم وصفاتهم المختلفة بتفصيل . ومن ثم فلا يكلف المسلم البحث عن شيء منها للإيمان به ، وإذا عثر عليها في بعض الأخبار أو الآثار فلا يجب الاعتقاد بموجبها . إذ لا يجب الاعتقاد إلا بما ثبت دليله من الدين بالقطع . وأما معرفة الصفات إجمالاً ، فلنا إلى العلم والاعتقاد بها سبيل لا تنكر . وسبيلنا إلى ذلك الخبر الصادق الوارد في كتاب الله عز وجل . فمن ذلك قوله تعالى : ﴿ لَنْ يَسْتَنْكِفَ الْمَسِيحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ عَبْدًا لِلَّهِ وَلا الْمَلائِكَةُ الْمُقَرَّبُونَ ﴾ [ النساء : ۱۷۲ ] وقوله عز وجل في وصف النار وخزنتها : ﴿ وَعَلَيْهَا مَلائِكَةٌ غِلاظٌ شِدَادٌ لا يَعْصُونَ اللَّهَ مَا أَمَرَهُمْ وَيَفْعَلُونَ مَا يُؤْمَرُونَ ﴾ [ التحريم : ٦ ] وقوله سبحانه : ﴿ وَقَالُوا اتَّخَذَ الرَّحْمَنُ وَلَدًا سُبْحَانَهُ بَلْ عِبَادٌ مُكْرَمُونَ لا يَسْبِقُونَهُ بِالْقَوْلِ وَهُمْ بِأَمْرِهِ يَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء : ٢٦-٢٧ ] وقوله عز وجل : ﴿ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ فَاطِرِ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضِ جَاعِلِ الْمَلائِكَةِ رُسُلاً أُولِي أَجْنِحَةٍ مَثْنَى وَثُلاثَ وَرُبَاعَ يَزِيدُ فِي الْخَلْقِ مَا يَشَاءُ إِنَّ اللَّهَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ [ فاطر : ١ ] .
As for their attributes, detailed speech concerning that is not possible, because they are among things that cannot be known except through reports, and no truthful, mutawātir reports have reached us that would reveal to us their states and various attributes in detail. Therefore, the Muslim is not required to research any of them in order to believe in them, and if he comes across some in certain reports or traditions, belief in accordance with them is not obligatory. For belief is only obligatory in what its proof from religion is established definitively. As for knowledge of the attributes in general, we have a way to know and believe in them that is not denied. And our way to that is the truthful report found in the Book of God – Mighty and Majestic. Among that is His statement – Exalted is He: {The Messiah would never disdain to be a servant of God, nor would the angels brought near} [An-Nisa 4:172], and His statement – Mighty and Majestic – in describing the Fire and its keepers: {Over it are angels, harsh and severe; they do not disobey God in what He commands them, but they do what they are commanded} [At-Tahrim 66:6], and His statement – Glorified is He: {And they say, 'The Most Merciful has taken a son.' Exalted is He! Rather, they are honored servants. They cannot precede Him in speech, and they act by His command} [Al-Anbiya 21:26-27], and His statement – Mighty and Majestic: {Praise be to God, the Originator of the heavens and the earth, who has made the angels messengers with wings – two, three, and four. He increases in creation what He wills. Indeed, God is over all things competent} [Fatir 35:1].
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a theological discussion on the epistemology of angelic attributes. The author distinguishes between detailed knowledge (tafṣīl) and general knowledge (ijmāl). He states that detailed knowledge is impossible because it depends on reports (akhbār), and no mutawātir reports have reached us that reveal their various states and attributes in detail. Therefore, Muslims are not required to research specific attributes for belief; if one encounters such details in non-mutawātir reports or traditions (āthār), they are not obligatory to believe. The principle is that belief is only obligatory for matters established by definitive proof (qaṭʻ). However, general knowledge of their attributes is attainable through the truthful report of the Quran. The author then provides four Quranic verses that describe general attributes: angels are not disdainful of worship (4:172), they are harsh keepers of Hell who obey God (66:6), they are honored servants who do not precede God in speech and act by His command (21:26-27), and they have wings and serve as messengers (35:1). These verses give a general but authoritative understanding of angelic nature without requiring detailed speculation.

إجمال
الخبر الصادق
القطع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Assuming that Muslims must believe in every reported detail about angels.
Correction: The author clarifies that only general attributes from definitive sources (like the Quran) are obligatory to believe.

Checkpoint

A) Because angels are not important
B) Because no mutawātir reports provide such detail
C) Because the Quran forbids speculation
D) Because attributes are unknowable

Key Takeaway
Muslims are only required to believe in the general attributes of angels as stated in definitive sources like the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Proof of the Existence of Angels and the Ruling on Denial
Author proves angel existence from Quran and Sunnah and states denial is kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the existence of angels is established by definitive proof from the Quran and Sunnah, and that denying their existence constitutes disbelief (kufr) by consensus and by logical implication.

Core Idea
Denying angels is disbelief because it rejects the Prophet's message and the Quran.

This lesson examines a key passage that establishes the definitive proof for the existence of angels. The author argues that numerous Quranic and Sunnah texts leave no room for doubt. He then explains the serious ruling that denial of angels is kufr, supported by both consensus and a Quranic verse. Understanding this helps us see why belief in the unseen is integral to faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the flow of the argument. Notice how the author moves from scriptural evidence to the ruling.
The passage is concise but packed with two proofs.
2
Identify the two proofs
Look for the two lines of evidence: first, explicit Quranic and hadith texts; second, the logical entailment that belief in prophethood requires belief in angels.
The second proof is linked to the first: the Prophet brought news of angels.
3
Understand the ruling
Recognize why denial is kufr: it contradicts the definitive proof and the consensus of Muslims. Also note the Quranic verse (an-Nisa 4:136) is cited as textual support.
The passage also ties denial of angels to denial of prophethood and the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي كل من القرآن والسنة الصحيحة نصوص كثيرة أخرى ، تخبر بصريح العبارة عن وجود الملائكة وبذلك تعلم أن وجودهم ثابت بدليل القطع الذي لا يمكن أن يلحقه شك أو ريب . ومن هنا كان إنكار وجودهم كفراً بإجماع المسلمين بل بنص قوله تعالى : وَمَن يَكْفر بالله وملائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ واليَومِ الآخِرِ فَقَد ضَلَّ ضَلالاً بعيداً ﴾ [ النساء : ١٣٦ ] على أن الإيمان بنبوة محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ونزول القرآن عليه يستلزم الإيمان بالملائكة ، فإنكار وجودهم إنكار للنبوة وللقرآن معاً
And in both the Quran and the authentic Sunnah there are many other texts that clearly inform of the existence of angels. By that you know that their existence is established by definitive proof that cannot be affected by any doubt or uncertainty. Hence, denial of their existence is disbelief by consensus of the Muslims, rather by the text of His statement: 'And whoever disbelieves in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, and the Last Day has certainly gone far astray' [an-Nisa 4:136]. Moreover, belief in the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) and the revelation of the Quran to him necessitates belief in the angels; thus, denial of their existence is denial of prophethood and the Quran together.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage proves the existence of angels and establishes the ruling that denying them is disbelief. The author begins by stating that numerous texts from the Quran and authentic Sunnah explicitly inform of the existence of angels. From these texts, we learn that their existence is established by definitive proof (dalil al-qat') that admits no doubt or suspicion. Therefore, denying the existence of angels constitutes kufr (disbelief) by the consensus of Muslims, and is further supported by the explicit Quranic verse (an-Nisa 4:136) which includes belief in angels among the pillars of faith. The author then adds a logical entailment: belief in the prophethood of Muhammad and the revelation of the Quran necessarily implies belief in angels, because the Prophet brought news of them. Hence, denying angels is equivalent to denying prophethood and the Quran itself.

Correction: This passage shows that belief in angels is a necessary part of faith; denial is kufr by consensus and by Quranic text, and it logically undermines belief in prophethood and the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The existence of angels is a definitive matter of faith; denying it is disbelief because it rejects the Prophet's message and the Quran.

The Epistemic Principle for Angel Attributes
Author states epistemic limitation for angel attributes and cites four Quranic verses as evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle that detailed knowledge of angels is not required, and that only summary knowledge through definitive revelation is sufficient for belief.

Core Idea
We only know what God tells us about angels.

Before exploring specific beliefs about angels, the author establishes an important rule: we cannot know their detailed attributes through reason or unreliable reports. Only definitive revelation—especially the Quran—provides trustworthy knowledge. This lesson examines that rule and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on epistemic principle
Read the Arabic passage and translation focusing on the first part about limitation of knowledge.
2
Distinguish detailed vs. summary knowledge
Notice the author says detailed knowledge (tafsil) is impossible, but summary knowledge (ijmal) is possible through revelation.
Key terms: تفصيل, إجمال
3
Understand the role of definitive proof
The author states belief is only required for what is proven definitively (qat') from religion.
Why does this matter? It prevents believing in unverified reports.
4
Examine the Quranic evidence
Read the four Quranic verses cited and see how they provide summary knowledge of angel attributes.
These verses are the foundation for the specific attributes discussed in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما صفاتهم، فإن تفصيل القول في ذلك مما لا سبيل إليه، إذ هي مما لا يمكن معرفته إلا عن طريق الأخبار، ولم يصل إلينا من الأخبار الصادقة المتواترة ما يكشف لنا عن أحوالهم وصفاتهم المختلفة بتفصيل . ومن ثم فلا يكلف المسلم البحث عن شيء منها للإيمان به، وإذا عثر عليها في بعض الأخبار أو الآثار فلا يجب الاعتقاد بموجبها . إذ لا يجب الاعتقاد إلا بما ثبت دليله من الدين بالقطع وأما معرفة الصفات إجمالاً، فلنا إلى العلم والاعتقاد بها سبيل لا تنكر . وسبيلنا إلى ذلك الخبر الصادق الوارد في كتاب الله عز وجل . فمن ذلك قوله تعالى : لن يَستَنكِفَ المَسيحُ أن يكون عبداً الله ولا الملائِكَةُ الْمُقَرَّبونَ .. [ النساء : ۱۷۲ ] وقوله عز وجل في وصف النار وخزنتها : و عَلَيْها مَلائكَةٌ غِلاظٌ شداد لا يعصونَ اللهَ ما أَمَرَهُمْ وَيَفعلون ما يؤمرون ﴾ [ التحريم : ٦ ] وقوله سبحانه : ( وقالوا اتَّخَذَ الرَّحْمنُ وَلَداً سُبْحانَهُ بَل عِبادٌ مُكْرَمونَ ، لا يسبقونه بالقول وهم بأمرِهِ يَعمَلونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء : ٢٦ ـ ٢٧ ] وقولـه عـز وجل : و الحمد الله فاطِرِ السَّمواتِ والأرض جاعِل الملائِكَةِ رُسُلاً أولي أجنحة مثنى وَثُلاثَ وَرُبَاعَ يَزيدُ في الخلق ما يَشاءُ إِنَّ اللهَ على كُلِّ شَيءٍ قَديرٌ ) [ فاطر : ١ ] . ومن ذلك ما ورد من الآيات والأحاديث التي تدل على أنهم منحوا القدرة على التشكل والظهور بأشكال مختلفة ، من مثل قوله جل جلاله : ﴿ فاتَّخَذَتْ من دونهم حجاباً فأرسلنا إليها روحنا فَتَمَثَّلَ لَهَا بَشَراً سَوِياً ﴾ [ مريم : ١٧ ] والأحاديث الكثيرة المختلفة التي تثبت أن النبي لم يلا كان يرى جبريل في هيئة رجل من الناس ، وأنه كثيراً ما كان يتمثل في شكل دحية الكلبي . فهذه الآيات وما يتبعها من أحاديث كثيرة صحيحة تؤيدها، توجب على المسلم أن يعتقد عقيدة جازمة بأن الملائكة يتصفون بالصفات التالية : ۱ - العبودية لله عز وجل ، فليسوا أولاداً ولا أنداداً له سبحانه وتعالى . ۲ - أنهم متقيدون بأوامر الله لهم ، فلا يعصون في أمر ولا ينحرفون إلى ارتكاب منهي ، وأنهم ملازمون لعبادته ، دأبهم ذكره والتسبيح بحمده ٣ - أن لهم أجنحة مثنى وثلاث ورباع، كما نص الخـالـق جـل جـلالـه على ذلك . وليس لنا أن نعلم شيئاً عن الصفات التفصيلية لهذه الأجنحة وكيفيتها ، إذ إنهم محجوبون عنا بإرادة الله وحكمه ، ولم يفصل القرآن الخبر عن ذلك ٤ - أنهم مع كونهم مخلوقين من نور غير مرئي بالعين ، فإن الله عز وجل قـد منحهم القدرة على التشكل والظهور بمظهر الأجسام الكثيفة المختلفة ولا يسع المؤمن بالله ورسوله إنكار شيء من هذه الصفات ، فإذا أنكرها أو أنكر شيئاً منها فإنه يكفر بذلك باتفاق
As for their attributes, detailed discussion of that is not possible, because they can only be known through reports, and no reliable mutawatir reports have reached us that reveal their states and various attributes in detail. Hence, the Muslim is not obligated to investigate any of them to believe in them; and if he comes across some of them in certain reports or traditions, he is not required to believe accordingly. For belief is only required in what has been established by definitive proof from religion. As for knowledge of the attributes in summary, we have a way to knowledge of and belief in them that is not denied. And our way to that is the truthful report contained in the Book of Allah, Almighty. Among that is His statement: 'The Messiah will never be disdainful to be a servant of Allah, nor the angels brought near' [an-Nisa 4:172]; and His statement describing the Fire and its keepers: 'And over it are angels, stern and severe; they do not disobey Allah in what He commands them but do what they are commanded' [at-Tahrim 66:6]; and His statement: 'And they say, "The Most Merciful has taken a son." Exalted is He! Rather, they are honored servants. They do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command' [al-Anbiya 21:26-27]; and His statement: '[All] praise is due to Allah, Creator of the heavens and the earth, [who] made the angels messengers having wings, two, three, and four. He increases in creation what He wills. Indeed, Allah is over all things competent' [Fatir 35:1]. And among that are the verses and hadiths that indicate that they have been given the ability to take form and appear in various shapes, such as His statement: 'So she took a screen apart from them, and We sent to her Our Spirit, and he appeared to her as a well-proportioned man' [Maryam 19:17], and the many various hadiths that establish that the Prophet used to see Jibril in the form of a man from among the people, and that he often appeared in the form of Dihya al-Kalbi. So these verses and the many authentic hadiths that support them oblige the Muslim to hold the firm belief that the angels are characterized by the following attributes: 1. Servitude to Allah Almighty; they are neither children nor rivals to Him. 2. They are bound by Allah's commands, so they do not disobey in any matter nor deviate to commit a forbidden act, and they are constant in His worship, their habit being remembrance of Him and glorification of His praise. 3. They have wings, two, three, and four, as the Creator stated. And we are not to know anything about the detailed attributes of these wings or their modality, for they are veiled from us by Allah's will and wisdom, and the Quran has not detailed that. 4. While they are created from light invisible to the eye, Allah has granted them the ability to take form and appear in the form of various dense bodies. And it is not permissible for the believer in Allah and His Messenger to deny any of these attributes; if he denies them or denies any of them, he thereby becomes a disbeliever by consensus.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the attributes of angels into a general epistemic principle and then a specific enumeration of four attributes confirmed by revelation. The author first establishes that detailed knowledge of angels' attributes is impossible because it depends on reports (akhbar) and no mutawatir reports have provided such detail. Therefore, the Muslim is not required to seek out or believe in any attribute unless it is established by definitive proof (qat'). However, we can know their attributes in summary (ijmāl) through the truthful reports in the Quran. The author then cites several Quranic verses: (1) an-Nisa 4:172 shows angels are servants of Allah. (2) at-Tahrim 66:6 shows they obey Allah perfectly. (3) al-Anbiya 21:26-27 shows they are honored servants who do not precede Allah in speech. (4) Fatir 35:1 shows they have wings. Additionally, Maryam 19:17 and hadith show they can take physical forms. From all these, the author derives four specific attributes: (1) servitude to Allah, not sonship or rivalry; (2) complete obedience and constant worship; (3) having wings (but we cannot know their details); (4) ability to take form. Denial of any of these attributes constitutes disbelief by consensus.

Key Terms
صفات الملائكة
الإجمال والتفصيل
الأخبار المتواترة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think we can know all details about angels through reason or any hadith.
Correction: The author clarifies that only definitive revelation (Quran, mutawatir) provides reliable knowledge; other reports are not required to believe.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for believing in a specific attribute of angels?
A) It must be mentioned in any hadith, regardless of authenticity.
B) It must be established by definitive proof from revelation.
C) It must be rationally conceivable.
D) It must be mentioned in both the Quran and Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Angels' detailed attributes are not known, but summary attributes from the Quran are sufficient for belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that detailed knowledge of angels is impossible. Have you ever spent time obsessing over questions about angels that God has not answered? What will you do to redirect that intellectual energy toward what He has revealed?
?
The author says belief is only required for what is established by definitive proof. Is your faith in the unseen based on God's definitive revelation, or have you allowed weak reports to shape your beliefs? Which of your current beliefs about angels might need re-examination?
?
When you read the four Quranic verses cited, do you truly let their meanings settle in your heart and change how you live? For example, knowing angels are ‘stern and severe’ in carrying out God’s commands—does that make you more serious about obeying Him? What one change will you make today because of this lesson?

The Four Specific Attributes of Angels
Author enumerates four specific attributes of angels from revelation and states the ruling on denying them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four specific attributes of angels derived from revelation and understand the consequence of denying them.

Core Idea
Angels are servants, obedient, have wings, and can change form.

After establishing the epistemic principle, the author now presents four specific attributes of angels that are firmly established by the Quran and authentic hadith. These attributes form part of what a Muslim must believe about angels. This lesson explores each attribute and the evidence for them.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration of attributes
Read the Arabic passage from the point about the ability to take form to the end. Identify the four attributes listed.
The attributes are numbered 1-4.
2
Examine the evidence for each attribute
For each attribute, note the Quranic verses or hadith cited as proof. Understand how the author derives each one.
The fourth attribute about taking form is supported by multiple hadith.
3
Understand the consequence of denial
The author concludes that denying any of these attributes leads to disbelief by consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Angels never disobey Allah, even for a moment. You sin daily and know it. Does this comparison humble you, or do you make excuses for your disobedience? How will you change your attitude toward sin after learning this?
?
You claim to be a servant of Allah, yet you feel entitled to question His commands when they don't suit you. The angels are true servants—they don't question. Will you repent from this entitlement and strive to be like them in submission?
?
If denying even one attribute of angels leads to disbelief, what does that say about the seriousness with which you take these teachings? Do you study these matters with the same urgency, or do you treat them as optional knowledge? Commit now to learning them properly.

Believing in Angels: Functions and Names from the Quran
Author states the epistemic rule for believing in angels' functions and names.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the epistemic limit of our knowledge about angels' functions and the obligation to believe only what the Quran explicitly reveals about them.

Core Idea
What the Quran reveals about angels is enough; the rest is not required.

This passage clarifies a key principle in Islamic creed regarding angels. While we cannot know the detailed functions of all angels through reason or tradition, the Quran provides us with some functions and names. Our belief must be firmly anchored in these revealed reports, without speculating beyond them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the structure: negative statement first, then positive obligation.
2
Identify the two key obligations
The passage states two obligations: belief in the functions mentioned in the Quran and belief in the names mentioned. Locate these in the text.
3
Reflect on the principle of sufficiency
Consider why the author emphasizes that no certain report exists for detailed functions. This teaches us to limit our knowledge to revelation and avoid speculation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما وظائفهم، فلا سبيل إلى معرفة هذه الوظائف بالتفصيل بالنسبة لجميع الملائكة . إذ لم يرد بذلك خبر يقيني يثبت به العلم . غير أن القرآن أخبرنا عن بعض هذه الوظائف، فيجب الإيمان بها طبقاً لبيانـه وأخباره؛ كما نص على أسماء بعضهم، فيجب الإيمان بهم بأسمائهم هذه
As for their functions, there is no way to know these functions in detail concerning all angels, because no certain report has come to establish knowledge of them. However, the Quran has informed us of some of these functions, so it is necessary to believe in them according to its explanation and reports; likewise, it has named some of them, so it is necessary to believe in them by these names.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage discusses the functions (waza'if) of angels and the limits of our knowledge about them. The author states that it is impossible to know the functions of all angels in detail, because no certain (yaqini) report has reached us that would establish such knowledge. However, the Quran has informed us of some functions, and we are obligated to believe in those functions as they are described. Similarly, the Quran has mentioned the names of some angels, and we are obligated to believe in them by those names. The passage does not list specific functions or names here; it merely establishes the epistemic rule: what is revealed must be believed, and what is not revealed is not required.

Key Terms
وظائف الملائكة
خبر يقيني
أسماء الملائكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the functions of angels that are not mentioned in the Quran?
A) They must be known through reason.
B) They are unknown and not required for belief.
C) They can be inferred from the functions of prophets.
D) They are all mentioned in hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the sole source of certain knowledge about angels' functions and names.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself imagining details about angels—their appearances, ranks, or daily tasks—that Allah has not revealed? What does this lesson teach you about the danger of such speculation? Will you commit to stopping it today?
?
The Quran tells us only a few functions and names of angels. Does your heart accept that this limited knowledge is sufficient for your faith, or do you secretly wish you knew more? How can you cultivate contentment with Allah's chosen revelation?
?
When you hear of people discussing elaborate stories about angels from questionable sources, do you feel pressured to accept them? How will you now respond, armed with the principle that only certain reports (like the Quran) obligate belief?

Two Functions of Angels: Recording and Protecting
Buti enumerates two functions of angels: recording deeds and protecting humans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two specific functions of angels according to the Quran: recording every word and protecting humans from harm.

Core Idea
Angels are both recorders of deeds and guardians of humans.

The Quran describes angels performing specific tasks that directly impact human life. In this lesson, we explore two of those tasks: the recording of every word and deed, and the protective guardianship over humans. Buti presents these functions with clear Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the two distinct functions mentioned and the Quranic verses cited for each.
Pay attention to the key terms: المتلقيان, المعقبة, الحفظة.
2
Identify the two functions and their proofs
Identify the first function (recording deeds) and the verse from Surah Qaf. Then identify the second function (protection) and the verses from Surah Ra'd and Surah An'am.
The author uses the pattern: function followed by scriptural evidence.
3
Reflect on personal accountability
Consider the implication that every word is recorded and that angels guard us. How does this affect your understanding of divine care and accountability?

ما اكتسبه من آثام ، تجد بيان ذلك في قوله تعالى : ﴿ إذ يَتَلَقَّى المتلقيان عن اليمين وَعَن الشّمالِ قَعِيدٌ مَا يَلْفِظُ مِنْ قَولٍ إِلا لَدَيهِ رَقِيبٌ عَتِيدٌ ﴾ [ ق : ١٧ - ١٨ ] . ومنها : المحافظة على الإنسان خلال مراحل حياته في مختلف شؤونه كلها وقد سمى الله تعالى الملائكة الذين وكل إليهم هذا الأمر بالمعقبة والحفظة ، فقال : لَهُ مُعَقبات مِن بَين يَدَيهِ وَمِن خَلْفِهِ يَحفَظُونَهُ ، من أمر الله ﴾ [ الرعد : ١١ ] وقال : ﴿ وَهوَ القاهِرُ فَوقَ عِبادِهِ ويُرْسِلُ عَلَيْكُمْ حَفَظَةٌ .. ﴾ [الأنعام : ٦١ ] .
What he has acquired of sins, you find its explanation in His saying, the Exalted: “When the two receivers receive, seated on the right and on the left. Not a word does he utter but there is a watcher by him ready [to record]” [Qaf 17-18]. And among them: preserving the human throughout the stages of his life in all his various affairs. And God, the Exalted, named the angels entrusted with this task al-mu'qibāt and al-ḥafazah, saying: “For him are angels in succession before him and behind him, guarding him by the command of God” [Ra'd 11]. And He said: “And He is the Subduer above His servants, and He sends over you guardians…” [An'am 61].
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof by Quranic citation of two functions of angels: (1) Recording deeds: Buti cites Surah Qaf 17-18, which mentions two angels (al-mutalaqqiyān) who receive and record every word a person utters. This function covers both good and evil deeds. (2) Protecting humans: Buti then cites Surah Ra'd 11 and Surah An'am 61, which refer to angels called al-mu'qibāt and al-ḥafazah. These angels guard humans from harm by God's command. The author follows a pattern: he states the function, then provides the scriptural evidence. The key terms here are al-mutalaqqiyān, al-mu'qibāt, and al-ḥafazah. The tone is didactic and evidence-based.

Misconception: Only bad deeds are recorded by angels.
Correction: The passage from Surah Qaf mentions 'every word' (plural), indicating both good and bad utterances are recorded.

B) Surah Qaf 17-18
C) Surah An'am 61

The Angel of Death: One or Many?
Buti discusses the Quranic evidence on whether the Angel of Death is one or a group.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic evidence regarding the Angel of Death and how the majority of scholars reconcile the apparent contradiction between the singular and plural references.

Core Idea
The Angel of Death is one angel aided by others, like a commander with troops.

The Quran mentions angels taking souls in two different ways: one verse uses 'messengers' (plural), another uses 'angel of death' (singular). Does this indicate a contradiction? Buti presents the question and shows how the majority of scholars understand these verses harmoniously. This lesson explores that resolution.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Notice how Buti frames the question.
Pay attention to the two Quranic verses cited.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
Find the verse from Surah An'am (6:61) that uses the plural 'messengers' and the verse from Surah Sajda (32:11) that uses 'the angel of death' in the singular.
These are the key evidence presented.
3
Understand the majority view
Read the commentary to grasp how the scholars reconcile the verses: the Angel of Death is one but is supported by a group of assisting angels.
The analogy of a commander and troops is used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : وظيفة قبض الأرواح . وهل أنيطت هذه الوظيفة بعدد من الملائكة أم بفرد واحد منهم ؟ لم يوضح القرآن الجواب على هذا ببيان قاطع ، فقد ذكر الله تعالى في آية من كتابه الكريم ما يدل على أنهم طائفة من الملائكة فقال : .. حتى إذا جاءَ أَحَدَكُمُ المَوتُ تَوَفَّتهُ رُسُلَنا وهم لا يُفَرِّطُونَ ) ( الأنعام : ٦١ ] . وذكر في آية أخرى ما يدل على أنه واحد فقط : لو قُل يَتوفَّاكُم مَلك الموتِ الَّذي وُكِّلَ بِكُم ثُمَّ إلى رَبِّكُم تُرجَعونَ ) [ السجدة : ١١ ] من والجمهور على أن ملك الموت واحد ، ولكن الله عز وجل عززه بطائفة أخرى الملائكة ، شأنها معه كشأن الجنود مع القائد .
And among them: the function of seizing souls. And is this function assigned to a number of angels or to a single individual among them? The Quran did not clarify the answer with a decisive statement. For God the Exalted mentioned in a verse of His Noble Book what indicates that they are a group of angels: “until when death comes to one of you, Our messengers take him, and they do not fail” [An'am 61]. And He mentioned in another verse what indicates that it is only one: “Say: The angel of death who has been entrusted with you will take you, then to your Lord you will be returned” [Sajda 11]. And the majority is that the angel of death is one, but God, Mighty and Majestic, strengthened him with another group of angels, their condition with him being like that of troops with a commander.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage presents a theological classification and resolution of a potential contradiction in the Quran regarding the Angel of Death. Buti identifies the third function of angels: taking souls (qabḍ al-arwāḥ). He then poses a question: is this task assigned to a single angel or a group? He notes that the Quran does not give a decisive answer. He cites two sets of verses: (1) Surah An'am 61 uses the plural 'messengers' (rusulunā), implying a group. (2) Surah Sajda 11 uses the singular 'angel of death' (malak al-mawt). Buti then states the majority view (al-jumhūr) that the Angel of Death is one individual, but God supports him with other angels, like a commander with troops. Thus, the apparent contradiction is resolved by distinguishing between the chief angel and his aides. The author follows a question-answer format, but here the answer is given as the established scholarly position.

Key Terms
وظيفة قبض الأرواح
ملك الموت
رسلنا
الجمهور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Quran contradicts itself regarding the Angel of Death.
Correction: The two verses are compatible: the Angel of Death is one chief angel, but he is aided by a group of angels, which explains the plural reference.

Checkpoint
How does Buti resolve the apparent contradiction between 'messengers' (plural) and 'angel of death' (singular) in the Quran?
A) He says the verses are abrogated.
B) He says the majority view is that there are multiple angels of death.
C) He says the Angel of Death is one, aided by other angels like a commander and troops.
D) He says the plural refers to different angels for different people.

Key Takeaway
The majority of scholars hold that the Angel of Death is one, but he is supported by other angels, like a commander with troops.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The Angel of Death is a commander with troops. Reflect on the order and precision of the universe. Are you living with the awareness that every moment of your life is accounted for by angels? What change can you make today to align more with your purpose?

Belief in Angels: Limits of Naming
Buti states that only Jibril is named in revelation, and naming Azrael is not obligatory belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that only Jibril is named in revelation regarding angels, and that naming other angels—like Azrael—is not an obligatory part of Islamic creed.

Core Idea
Only Jibril is named in revelation; other angel names are not obligatory.

In this lesson, Buti clarifies a crucial point about what Muslims must believe regarding angels. While we affirm that God has assigned specific tasks to groups of angels, the names of most angels are not revealed in the Qur'an or authentic hadith. The only name explicitly given is Jibril (Gabriel). This passage helps us distinguish between what is required to believe and what is merely mentioned in weaker traditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice that Buti begins by stating what revelation has disclosed about angel names.
Pay attention to the phrase 'except Jibril'.
2
Identify the obligatory belief
Buti says the Muslim must know and believe that God has entrusted tasks to groups of angels, but their names and attributes are known only to God.
This is the core of what is obligatory: affirming the existence and roles, not the names.
3
Understand the ruling on Azrael
The name 'Azrael' for the Angel of Death appears in some traditions, but Buti states these do not reach the level of obligatory belief. This means it is not required to affirm that name as part of one's faith.
It is not forbidden to use the name, but it is not an article of faith.
4
Reflect on the principle
Consider the broader principle: we should not add to the obligatory beliefs beyond what revelation has made clear. This protects the creed from unverified reports.
This reflects a cautious, text-based approach to theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا وأنت ترى أن النصوص لم تكشف عن أسماء هؤلاء الملائكة الذين وكل الله إليهم هذه الأمور المختلفة التي ذكرناها ما عدا جبريل . فالذي يجب على المسلم معرفته والاعتقاد بموجبه هو أن الله عز وجل قد أناط هذه الوظائف المختلفة بجماعات من الملائكة ، الله أعلم بأسمائهم وخصائصهم . وتسمية ملك الموت بعزرائيل شيء دلت عليه آثار مختلفة لم تصل من القوة إلى درجة وجوب الاعتقاد .
This, and you see that the texts have not disclosed the names of these angels whom God entrusted with these different matters we have mentioned, except Jibril. So what is obligatory for the Muslim to know and believe accordingly is that God, Mighty and Majestic, has assigned these various functions to groups of angels; God knows best their names and attributes. And naming the Angel of Death as 'Azrael' is something indicated by various traditions that have not reached the level of obligatory belief.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion and a ruling (ḥukm) regarding what Muslims must believe about angels. Buti first notes that revelation (al-nuṣūṣ) has not named the angels assigned to the functions he listed (recording, protection, taking souls) except for Jibril (Gabriel). He then deduces the obligatory belief: the Muslim must affirm that God entrusted these tasks to groups of angels, while leaving their specific names and attributes to God's knowledge (allāhu a'lam). The naming of the Angel of Death as 'Azrael' is addressed separately: Buti states that various reports (āthār) mention this name, but these reports are not strong enough to make belief in that name obligatory (darajat wujūb al-i'tiqād). This implies that while it is not forbidden to use the name, one should not consider it a required article of faith. The tone is cautious, emphasizing the limits of revealed knowledge.

Key Terms
النصوص
جبريل
عزرائيل
وجوب الاعتقاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Muslims believe that naming the Angel of Death as 'Azrael' is an obligatory part of faith.
Correction: Buti clarifies that this name comes from traditions that are not strong enough to make belief in it obligatory. It is not a required article of creed.

Checkpoint
